</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Andhra Pradesh</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/ɑː/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">ɑː</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;p&#39; in &#39;pie&#39;">p</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/ɛ/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">ɛ</span><span title="/ʃ/: &#39;sh&#39; in &#39;shy&#39;">ʃ</span></span>/</a></span></span>) (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Andhra_pradesh.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/39/Andhra_pradesh.ogg" class="internal" title="Andhra pradesh.ogg">pronunciation</a></span>&#160;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Andhra_pradesh.ogg" title="File:Andhra pradesh.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>) is one of the 29 <a href="/wiki/States_and_union_territories_of_India" title="States and union territories of India">states of India</a>. Situated in the south-east of the country, it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_and_union_territories_of_India_by_area" title="List of states and union territories of India by area">seventh-largest state</a> in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, covering an area of 160,205&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (61,855&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-profile_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-profile-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> As per the <a href="/wiki/2011_Census_of_India" title="2011 Census of India">2011 census</a>, it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_and_union_territories_of_India_by_population" title="List of states and union territories of India by population">tenth-most populous</a> state, with 49,386,799 inhabitants. The largest city in Andhra Pradesh is <a href="/wiki/Visakhapatnam" title="Visakhapatnam">Visakhapatnam</a>. <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">Telugu</a>, one of the <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_India#Classical" title="Languages of India">classical languages of India</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Classical_Language_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Classical_Language-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> is the major and official language of Andhra Pradesh.<sup id="cite_ref-language_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-language-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nclmanurep2010_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nclmanurep2010-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The north-western portion of Andhra Pradesh was separated to form the new state of <a href="/wiki/Telangana" title="Telangana">Telangana</a> on 2 June 2014, and <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad" title="Hyderabad">Hyderabad</a>, the longtime capital of Andhra Pradesh, was transferred to Telangana as part of the division. However, in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh_Reorganisation_Act,_2014" title="Andhra Pradesh Reorganisation Act, 2014">Andhra Pradesh Reorganisation Act, 2014</a>, Hyderabad was to remain the acting capital of both Andhra Pradesh and Telangana states for a period of time not exceeding ten years.<sup id="cite_ref-reorganisation_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reorganisation-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The new <a href="/wiki/Riverfront" title="Riverfront">riverfront</a> <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> capital, <a href="/wiki/Amaravati" title="Amaravati">Amaravati</a>, is under the jurisdiction of the <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh_Capital_Region_Development_Authority" title="Andhra Pradesh Capital Region Development Authority">Andhra Pradesh Capital Region Development Authority</a> (APCRDA).<sup id="cite_ref-amaravati_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amaravati-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Andhra Pradesh has a <a href="/wiki/Coastline" class="mw-redirect" title="Coastline">coastline</a> of 974&#160;km (605&#160;mi) – the second-longest coastline among the states of India, after <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> – with jurisdiction over almost 15,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> of territorial waters.<sup id="cite_ref-profile_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-profile-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The state is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Telangana" title="Telangana">Telangana</a> in the north-west, <a href="/wiki/Chhattisgarh" title="Chhattisgarh">Chhattisgarh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Odisha" title="Odisha">Odisha</a> in the north-east, <a href="/wiki/Karnataka" title="Karnataka">Karnataka</a> in the west, <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu">Tamil Nadu</a> in the south, and to the east lies the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a>. The small enclave of <a href="/wiki/Yanam_district" title="Yanam district">Yanam</a>, a district of <a href="/wiki/Puducherry" title="Puducherry">Puducherry</a>, lies to the south of <a href="/wiki/Kakinada" title="Kakinada">Kakinada</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Godavari_River" title="Godavari River">Godavari</a> delta on the eastern side of the state.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The state is made up of the two major regions of <a href="/wiki/Rayalaseema" title="Rayalaseema">Rayalaseema</a>, in the inland southwestern part of the state, and <a href="/wiki/Coastal_Andhra" title="Coastal Andhra">Coastal Andhra</a> to the east and northeast, bordering the Bay of Bengal.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The state comprises thirteen districts in total, nine of which are located in Coastal Andhra and four in Rayalaseema. The largest city and commercial hub of the state are <a href="/wiki/Visakhapatnam" title="Visakhapatnam">Visakhapatnam</a>, located on the Bay of Bengal, with a GDP of <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>43.5&#160;billion; the second largest city in the state is <a href="/wiki/Vijayawada" title="Vijayawada">Vijayawada</a>, located on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Krishna_River" title="Krishna River">Krishna River</a>, which has a GDP of US&#160;billion (as of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Andhra_Pradesh" title="Economy of Andhra Pradesh">economy of Andhra Pradesh</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indian_states_and_union_territories_by_GDP" title="List of Indian states and union territories by GDP">ninth-largest state economy</a> in India with <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>8.10 lakh crore</span> (US$120&#160;billion) in <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> and a per capita GDP of <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>144,000</span> (US$2,100).<sup id="cite_ref-MOSPI_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOSPI-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Andhra Pradesh ranks <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indian_states_and_territories_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of Indian states and territories by Human Development Index">twentieth</a> among Indian states in <a href="/wiki/Human_development_index" class="mw-redirect" title="Human development index">human development index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-snhdi-gdl_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snhdi-gdl-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Andhra Pradesh hosted 121.8 million visitors in 2015, a 30% growth in tourist arrivals over the previous year,<sup id="cite_ref-The_Hindu_Business_Line_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Hindu_Business_Line-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> making it the <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_India#Statistics" title="Tourism in India">third most-visited</a> state in India. The <a href="/wiki/Venkateswara_Temple,_Tirumala" title="Venkateswara Temple, Tirumala">Tirumala Venkateswara Temple</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tirupati" title="Tirupati">Tirupati</a> is one of the world's most visited religious sites, with 18.25 million visitors per year.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Other <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Andhra_Pradesh#Religious_and_pilgrimage_sites" title="Tourism in Andhra Pradesh">pilgrimage centres</a> in the state include the <a href="/wiki/Mallikarjuna_Jyotirlinga" title="Mallikarjuna Jyotirlinga">Mallikarjuna Jyotirlinga</a> at <a href="/wiki/Srisailam" title="Srisailam">Srisailam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Srikalahasteeswara_temple" title="Srikalahasteeswara temple">Srikalahasteeswara Temple</a> at <a href="/wiki/Srikalahasti" title="Srikalahasti">Srikalahasti</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ameen_Peer_Dargah" title="Ameen Peer Dargah">Ameen Peer Dargah</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kadapa" title="Kadapa">Kadapa</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Amaravathi_Mahachaitya" class="mw-redirect" title="Amaravathi Mahachaitya">Mahachaitya</a> at <a href="/wiki/Amaravathi_(village),_Guntur_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Amaravathi (village), Guntur district">Amaravathi</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kanaka_Durga_Temple" title="Kanaka Durga Temple">Kanaka Durga Temple</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vijayawada" title="Vijayawada">Vijayawada</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Prasanthi_Nilayam" title="Prasanthi Nilayam">Prasanthi Nilayam</a> in <a href="/wiki/Puttaparthi" title="Puttaparthi">Puttaparthi</a>. The state's <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Andhra_Pradesh#Nature_tourism" title="Tourism in Andhra Pradesh">natural attractions</a> include the <a href="/wiki/Tourist_attractions_in_Visakhapatnam#Beaches" class="mw-redirect" title="Tourist attractions in Visakhapatnam">beaches</a> of <a href="/wiki/Visakhapatnam" title="Visakhapatnam">Visakhapatnam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hill_station" title="Hill station">hill stations</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Araku_Valley" title="Araku Valley">Araku Valley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Horsley_Hills" title="Horsley Hills">Horsley Hills</a>, and the island of <a href="/wiki/Konaseema" title="Konaseema">Konaseema</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Godavari_River" title="Godavari River">Godavari River</a> delta.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Andhra_Pradesh" title="History of Andhra Pradesh">History of Andhra Pradesh</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Toponomy">Toponomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Toponomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A group of people named Andhras was mentioned in <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> texts such as <a href="/wiki/Aitareya_Brahmana" title="Aitareya Brahmana">Aitareya Brahmana</a> (800–500 <a href="/wiki/BCE" class="mw-redirect" title="BCE">BCE</a>). According to <i>Aitareya Brahmana</i> of the <a href="/wiki/Rig_Veda" class="mw-redirect" title="Rig Veda">Rig Veda</a>, the Andhras left north India from banks of <a href="/wiki/River_Yamuna" class="mw-redirect" title="River Yamuna">River Yamuna</a> and settled in south India.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The Satavahanas have been mentioned by the names <i>Andhra</i>, <i>Andhrara-jateeya</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Andhrabhrtya" title="Andhrabhrtya">Andhrabhrtya</a></i> in the <a href="/wiki/Puranas" title="Puranas">Puranic literature</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SNS_1999_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SNS_1999-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SC_1974_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SC_1974-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> They did not refer themselves as <i>Andhra</i> in any of their coins or inscriptions; it is possible that they were termed as Andhras because of their ethnicity or because their territory included the Andhra region.<sup id="cite_ref-SEA_2001_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SEA_2001-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_and_medieval_history">Early and medieval history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early and medieval history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Telugu_talli_bomma.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Telugu_talli_bomma.JPG/220px-Telugu_talli_bomma.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Telugu_talli_bomma.JPG/330px-Telugu_talli_bomma.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Telugu_talli_bomma.JPG/440px-Telugu_talli_bomma.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Telugu_talli_bomma.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Telugu Thalli</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Assaka" title="Assaka">Assaka Mahajanapada</a>, one of the sixteen Vedic Mahajanapadas, included Andhra, <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra" title="Maharashtra">Maharashtra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telangana" title="Telangana">Telangana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Archaeological evidence from places such as <a href="/wiki/Amaravathi_(village),_Guntur_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Amaravathi (village), Guntur district">Amaravati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dharanikota" title="Dharanikota">Dharanikota</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vaddamanu" title="Vaddamanu">Vaddamanu</a> suggests that the Andhra region was part of the <a href="/wiki/Mauryan_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Mauryan Empire">Mauryan Empire</a>. Amaravati might have been a regional centre for the Mauryan rule. After the death of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Ashoka" title="Ashoka">Ashoka</a>, Mauryan rule weakened around 200 BCE and was replaced by several smaller <a href="/wiki/Kingship_and_kingdom_of_God" title="Kingship and kingdom of God">kingdoms</a> in the Andhra region.<sup id="cite_ref-Akira_2012_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Akira_2012-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Satavahana_dynasty" title="Satavahana dynasty">Satavahana dynasty</a> dominated the <a href="/wiki/Deccan_Plateau" title="Deccan Plateau">Deccan region</a> from the <a href="/wiki/1st_century_BC" title="1st century BC">1st century BC</a> to the <a href="/wiki/3rd_century" title="3rd century">3rd century</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CH_2009_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CH_2009-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The later Satavahanas made <a href="/wiki/Dharanikota" title="Dharanikota">Dharanikota</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amaravathi_village,_Guntur_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Amaravathi village, Guntur district">Amaravathi</a> their capital, which according to the Buddhists is the place where <a href="/wiki/Nagarjuna" title="Nagarjuna">Nagarjuna</a>, the philosopher of <a href="/wiki/Mahayana" title="Mahayana">Mahayana</a> lived in the 2nd and 3rd centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Ikshvaku" title="Andhra Ikshvaku">Andhra Ikshvakus</a>, with their capital at <a href="/wiki/Vijayapuri_(South)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vijayapuri (South)">Vijayapuri</a>, succeeded the Satavahanas in the <a href="/wiki/Krishna_River" title="Krishna River">Krishna River</a> valley in the latter half of the 2nd century.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Pallavas, who were originally executive officers under the Satavahana kings, were not a recognised political power before the 2nd century AD and were swept away by the <a href="/wiki/Western_Chalukya_Empire" title="Western Chalukya Empire">Western Chalukyan</a> invasion, led by Pulakesin II in the first quarter of the 7th century CE.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> After the downfall of the Ikshvakus, the <a href="/wiki/Vishnukundinas" class="mw-redirect" title="Vishnukundinas">Vishnukundinas</a> were the first great dynasty in the 5th and 6th centuries, and held sway over the entire Andhra country, including <a href="/wiki/Kalinga_(historical_region)" title="Kalinga (historical region)">Kalinga</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/Telangana" title="Telangana">Telangana</a>. They played an important role in the history of Deccan during the 5th and 6th century CE, with <a href="/wiki/Eluru" title="Eluru">Eluru</a>, Amaravathi and Puranisangam.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Salankayanas" class="mw-redirect" title="Salankayanas">Salankayanas</a> were an ancient dynasty that ruled the Andhra region between Godavari and Krishna with their capital at Vengi (modern <a href="/wiki/Pedavegi" title="Pedavegi">Pedavegi</a>) from 300 to 440 CE.<sup id="cite_ref-Ancient_Indian_History_and_civilization_By_S._N._Sen_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ancient_Indian_History_and_civilization_By_S._N._Sen-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Chalukyas" title="Eastern Chalukyas">Eastern Chalukyas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Vengi" title="Vengi">Vengi</a>, whose dynasty lasted for around five hundred years from the 7th century until 1130 C.E., eventually merged with the <a href="/wiki/Chola_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Chola empire">Chola empire</a>. They continued to rule under the protection of the Chola empire until 1189 C.E. when the kingdom succumbed to the <a href="/wiki/Hoysalas" class="mw-redirect" title="Hoysalas">Hoysalas</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Yadavas" class="mw-redirect" title="Yadavas">Yadavas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The roots of the <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">Telugu language</a> have been seen on inscriptions found near the <a href="/wiki/Guntur" title="Guntur">Guntur</a> district and from others dating to the rule of Renati Cholas in the fifth century <a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">CE</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kakatiyas" class="mw-redirect" title="Kakatiyas">Kakatiyas</a> ruled Andhra Pradesh state for nearly two hundred years and constructed several forts. They were succeeded by the <a href="/wiki/Musunuri_Nayaks" class="mw-redirect" title="Musunuri Nayaks">Musunuri Nayaks</a>. Musunuri Nayaks led a confederation of nayakas to overthrow the rule of the Delhi Sultanate in Telugu lands.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Reddi_kingdom" title="Reddi kingdom">Reddi Kingdom</a> (1325–1448 CE) was established by Prolaya Vema Reddi in the early <a href="/wiki/14th_century" title="14th century">14th century</a>, who ruled from present day Kondaveedu. Prolaya Vema Reddi was part of the confederation of states that started a movement against the invading <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic</a> Muslim armies of the <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Sultanate" title="Delhi Sultanate">Delhi Sultanate</a>. They constructed <a href="/wiki/Kondaveedu_Fort" title="Kondaveedu Fort">Kondaveedu Fort</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>, which they ruled between 1328–1428, before it was taken over by the <a href="/wiki/Gajapathi_King" class="mw-redirect" title="Gajapathi King">Gajpathis</a> of Orissa, and later ravaged by the <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> rulers of the <a href="/wiki/Bahmani_kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahmani kingdom">Bahmani kingdom</a> in 1458. The <a href="/wiki/Vijayanagara" title="Vijayanagara">Vijayanagara</a> emperor <a href="/wiki/Krishnadevaraya" title="Krishnadevaraya">Krishnadevaraya</a> captured it in 1516. The <a href="/wiki/Golconda" class="mw-redirect" title="Golconda">Golconda</a> <a href="/wiki/Sultan" title="Sultan">Sultans</a> fought for the fort in 1531, 1536 and 1579, and Sultan <a href="/wiki/Quli_Qutb_Shah" class="mw-redirect" title="Quli Qutb Shah">Quli Qutb Shah</a> captured it in 1579, renaming it <i>Murtuzanagar</i>. It was reconquered by Vijayanagara who overthrew sultanate rule across the entirety of modern-day Andhra Pradesh (excluding Telangana). After this rebellion, the Bahmani sultans launched no further military campaigns outside their kingdoms, because the Marathas soon emerged as the strongest power in India.<sup id="cite_ref-gazette_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gazette-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sewell_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sewell-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gallery_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gallery-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Efforts are in progress to classify <a href="/wiki/Kondaveedu_Fort" title="Kondaveedu Fort">Kondaveedu Fort</a> as a UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Raaja_mahal_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Raaja_mahal_1.JPG/220px-Raaja_mahal_1.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Raaja_mahal_1.JPG/330px-Raaja_mahal_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Raaja_mahal_1.JPG/440px-Raaja_mahal_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Raaja_mahal_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rajmahal of <a href="/wiki/Chandragiri" title="Chandragiri">Chandragiri</a> Fort</div></div></div>
<p>The Vijayanagara Empire originated in the <a href="/wiki/Deccan_Plateau" title="Deccan Plateau">Deccan Plateau</a> region in the early 14th century. It was established in 1336 by <a href="/wiki/Harihara_Raya_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Harihara Raya I">Harihara Raya I</a> and his brother <a href="/wiki/Bukka_Raya_I" title="Bukka Raya I">Bukka Raya I</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Sangama_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Sangama Dynasty">Sangama Dynasty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Book_of_Duarte_Barbosa_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Book_of_Duarte_Barbosa-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_madras_journal_of_literature_and_science,_year_1882_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_madras_journal_of_literature_and_science,_year_1882-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The empire's patronage enabled fine arts and literature to reach new heights in <a href="/wiki/Kannada_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kannada language">Kannada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">Telugu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Carnatic_music" title="Carnatic music">Carnatic music</a> evolved into its current form.<sup id="cite_ref-Kannadaempire_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kannadaempire-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> During the Vijayanagara Empire, the <a href="/wiki/Pemmasani_Nayaks" title="Pemmasani Nayaks">Pemmasani Nayaks</a> controlled parts of Andhra Pradesh and had large mercenary armies that were the vanguard of the <a href="/wiki/Vijayanagara_Empire" title="Vijayanagara Empire">Vijayanagara Empire</a> in the sixteenth century.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lepakshi" title="Lepakshi">Lepakshi</a> group of monuments are culturally and archaeologically significant as it is the location of shrines dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Shiva" title="Shiva">Shiva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vishnu" title="Vishnu">Vishnu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Veerabhadra_Temple,_Lepakshi" title="Veerabhadra Temple, Lepakshi">Veerabhadra</a> which were built during the <a href="/wiki/Vijayanagara_Empire" title="Vijayanagara Empire">Vijayanagara</a> Kings' period (1336–1646). The temples are the location of mural paintings of the Vijayanagara kings, Dravidian art, and inscriptions. Near the temple complex is a large granite <a href="/wiki/Nandi_bull" class="mw-redirect" title="Nandi bull">Nandi bull</a>. On a hillock known as <i>Kurma Saila</i> ('tortoise-shaped hill') are other temples to Papanatheswara, <a href="/wiki/Raghunatha" title="Raghunatha">Raghunatha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rama" title="Rama">Srirama</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Durga" title="Durga">Durga</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-deccanchronicle.com_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deccanchronicle.com-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Government of Andhra Pradesh has taken the initiative for including the "Lepakshi Group of Monuments" among the <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_India" title="List of World Heritage Sites in India">UNESCO World Heritage sites in India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_history">Modern history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Modern history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Harihara" title="Harihara">Harihara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bukka" class="mw-redirect" title="Bukka">Bukka</a>, who served as treasury officers of the Kakatiyas of Warangal, founded the <a href="/wiki/Vijayanagara_Empire" title="Vijayanagara Empire">Vijayanagara Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In 1347 <a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">CE</a>, an independent Muslim state, the <a href="/wiki/Bahmani_Sultanate" title="Bahmani Sultanate">Bahmani Sultanate</a>, was established in <a href="/wiki/South_India" title="South India">south India</a> by <a href="/wiki/Ala-ud-Din_Bahman_Shah" title="Ala-ud-Din Bahman Shah">Ala-ud-Din Bahman Shah</a> in a revolt against the Delhi Sultanate. The <a href="/wiki/Qutb_Shahi_dynasty" title="Qutb Shahi dynasty">Qutb Shahi dynasty</a> held sway over the Andhra country for about two hundred years from the early part of the sixteenth century to the end of the seventeenth century.<sup id="cite_ref-Richards_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Richards-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the early nineteenth century, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Circars" title="Northern Circars">Northern Circars</a> was ceded to the British East India Company and became part of the <a href="/wiki/Madras_Presidency" title="Madras Presidency">Madras Presidency</a>. Eventually, this region emerged as the <a href="/wiki/Coastal_Andhra" title="Coastal Andhra">Coastal Andhra</a> region. Later the <a href="/wiki/Nizam" class="mw-redirect" title="Nizam">Nizam</a> rulers of Hyderabad ceded five territories to the British that eventually became the <a href="/wiki/Rayalaseema" title="Rayalaseema">Rayalaseema</a> region. The Nizams retained control of the interior provinces as the <a href="/wiki/Princely_state" title="Princely state">princely state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad_State" title="Hyderabad State">Hyderabad</a>, acknowledging British rule in return for local autonomy. However, <a href="/wiki/Komaram_Bheem" title="Komaram Bheem">Komaram Bheem</a>, a tribal leader, started his fight against the erstwhile <a href="/wiki/Asaf_Jahi_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Asaf Jahi Dynasty">Asaf Jahi Dynasty</a> for the liberation of <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad_State" title="Hyderabad State">Hyderabad State</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French</a> occupied <a href="/wiki/Yanam_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="Yanam (India)">Yanam</a>, in the Godavari delta, and (save for periods of British control) would hold it until 1954. In 1947 Vizianagaram was the largest Hindu princely state in Andhra Pradesh.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">India became independent</a> from the United Kingdom in 1947. The Nizam wanted to retain the independence of the Princely Hyderabad State from India, but the people of the region launched a movement to join the Indian Union. The state of Hyderabad was forcibly joined to the Republic of India with <a href="/wiki/Operation_Polo" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Polo">Operation Polo</a> in 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-independence">Post-independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Post-independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Andhra_State" title="Andhra State">Andhra State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vishalandhra_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Vishalandhra Movement">Vishalandhra Movement</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Combined_Andhra_Pradesh" title="Combined Andhra Pradesh">Combined Andhra Pradesh</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Archaeological_Museums_map_of_Andhra_Pradesh.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Archaeological_Museums_map_of_Andhra_Pradesh.png/220px-Archaeological_Museums_map_of_Andhra_Pradesh.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Archaeological_Museums_map_of_Andhra_Pradesh.png/330px-Archaeological_Museums_map_of_Andhra_Pradesh.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Archaeological_Museums_map_of_Andhra_Pradesh.png/440px-Archaeological_Museums_map_of_Andhra_Pradesh.png 2x" data-file-width="923" data-file-height="881" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Archaeological_Museums_map_of_Andhra_Pradesh.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Archaeological Museums map of Andhra Pradesh</div></div></div>
<p>In an effort to gain an independent state based on linguistic identity, and to protect the interests of the Telugu-speaking people of <a href="/wiki/Madras_State" title="Madras State">Madras State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potti_Sreeramulu" title="Potti Sreeramulu">Potti Sreeramulu</a> fasted to death in 1952. As Madras became a bone of contention, in 1949 a JVP committee report stated: "Andhra Province could be formed provided the Andhras give up their claim on the city of Madras (now Chennai)". After Potti Sreeramulu's death, the Telugu-speaking area of <a href="/wiki/Andhra_State" title="Andhra State">Andhra State</a> was carved out of <a href="/wiki/Madras_State" title="Madras State">Madras State</a> on 1 October 1953, with <a href="/wiki/Kurnool" title="Kurnool">Kurnool</a> as its capital city.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> On the basis of the <a href="/wiki/Gentlemen%27s_Agreement_of_1956" title="Gentlemen&#39;s Agreement of 1956">gentlemen's agreement</a> of 1 November 1956, the <a href="/wiki/States_Reorganisation_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="States Reorganisation Act">States Reorganisation Act</a> formed <a href="/wiki/Combined_Andhra_Pradesh" title="Combined Andhra Pradesh">combined Andhra Pradesh</a> by merging Andhra State with the Telugu-speaking areas of the already existing <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad_State" title="Hyderabad State">Hyderabad State</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Know_Hyderabad_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Know_Hyderabad-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Hyderabad was made the capital of the new state. The Marathi-speaking areas of Hyderabad State merged with <a href="/wiki/Bombay_State" title="Bombay State">Bombay State</a> and the Kannada-speaking areas were merged with <a href="/wiki/Mysore_State" title="Mysore State">Mysore State</a>.
</p><p>In February 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh_Reorganisation_Act,_2014" title="Andhra Pradesh Reorganisation Act, 2014">Andhra Pradesh Reorganisation Act, 2014</a> bill was passed by the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_India" title="Parliament of India">Parliament of India</a> for the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Telangana" title="Telangana">Telangana</a> state comprising <a href="/wiki/List_of_districts_in_Telangana" title="List of districts in Telangana">ten districts</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad" title="Hyderabad">Hyderabad</a> will remain as a joint capital for not exceeding ten years.<sup id="cite_ref-reorganisation_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reorganisation-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The new state of Telangana came into existence on 2 June 2014 after approval from the <a href="/wiki/President_of_India" title="President of India">President of India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Number of petitions questioning the validity of Andhra Pradesh Reorganisation Act, 2014 is long pending for the verdict since April 2014 before the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_court_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme court of India">supreme court</a> constitutional bench.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Andhra_Pradesh" title="Geography of Andhra Pradesh">Geography of Andhra Pradesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_districts_of_Andhra_Pradesh" class="mw-redirect" title="List of districts of Andhra Pradesh">List of districts of Andhra Pradesh</a></div>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 157.33333333333px"><div style="width: 157.33333333333px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 155.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Andhra_Pradesh_and_Telangana_Physical.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Andhra_Pradesh_and_Telangana_Physical.jpeg/233px-Andhra_Pradesh_and_Telangana_Physical.jpeg" decoding="async" width="156" height="134" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Andhra_Pradesh_and_Telangana_Physical.jpeg/350px-Andhra_Pradesh_and_Telangana_Physical.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Andhra_Pradesh_and_Telangana_Physical.jpeg/465px-Andhra_Pradesh_and_Telangana_Physical.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2598" data-file-height="2244" /></a></div></div>

</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 163.33333333333px"><div style="width: 163.33333333333px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 161.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ap-districts.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Ap-districts.png/242px-Ap-districts.png" decoding="async" width="162" height="134" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Ap-districts.png/364px-Ap-districts.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Ap-districts.png/484px-Ap-districts.png 2x" data-file-width="2485" data-file-height="2064" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">

</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 180.66666666667px"><div style="width: 180.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 178.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Srisailam_Dam_and_River_Krishna.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Srisailam_Dam_and_River_Krishna.jpg/268px-Srisailam_Dam_and_River_Krishna.jpg" decoding="async" width="179" height="134" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Srisailam_Dam_and_River_Krishna.jpg/403px-Srisailam_Dam_and_River_Krishna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Srisailam_Dam_and_River_Krishna.jpg/536px-Srisailam_Dam_and_River_Krishna.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Krishna_River" title="Krishna River">Krishna River</a> at Srisailam
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul>
<p>The state has varied <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">topography</a> ranging from the hills of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Ghats" title="Eastern Ghats">Eastern Ghats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nallamala_Hills" title="Nallamala Hills">Nallamala Hills</a> to the shores of <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a> that supports varied ecosystems, the rich diversity of flora and fauna. There are two main rivers namely, <a href="/wiki/Krishna_River" title="Krishna River">Krishna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Godavari_river" class="mw-redirect" title="Godavari river">Godavari</a>, that flow through the state. The coast of the state extends along the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a> from <a href="/wiki/Srikakulam_district" title="Srikakulam district">Srikakulam</a> to <a href="/wiki/Nellore_district" title="Nellore district">Nellore district</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-coastline_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coastline-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The plains to the east of Eastern Ghats form the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_coastal_plains" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern coastal plains">Eastern coastal plains</a>. The coastal plains are for the most part of delta regions formed by the Godavari, Krishna, and <a href="/wiki/Penner_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Penner River">Penner Rivers</a>. The Eastern Ghats are discontinuous and individual sections have local names. The Eastern Ghats are a major dividing line in the state's geography. The Kadapa Basin<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (January 2016)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> formed by two arching branches of the Eastern Ghats is a mineral-rich area. The Ghats become more pronounced towards the south and extreme north of the coast. Most of the coastal plains are put to intense agricultural use. The <a href="/wiki/Rayalaseema" title="Rayalaseema">Rayalaseema</a> region has semi-arid conditions.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_vegetation_and_conservation">Natural vegetation and conservation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Natural vegetation and conservation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Natural_vegetation_and_Wildlife_of_Andhra_Pradesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural vegetation and Wildlife of Andhra Pradesh">Natural vegetation and Wildlife of Andhra Pradesh</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pichavaram_Mangrove_Forest.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Pichavaram_Mangrove_Forest.jpg/220px-Pichavaram_Mangrove_Forest.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Pichavaram_Mangrove_Forest.jpg/330px-Pichavaram_Mangrove_Forest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Pichavaram_Mangrove_Forest.jpg/440px-Pichavaram_Mangrove_Forest.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6979" data-file-height="4655" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pichavaram_Mangrove_Forest.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mangrove forest near Kakinada</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh_Forest_Department" title="Andhra Pradesh Forest Department">Andhra Pradesh Forest Department</a> deals with protection, conservation and management of <a href="/wiki/Forests" class="mw-redirect" title="Forests">forests</a>. The total forest cover of the state after the bifurcation is left with an area of 22,862&#160;km<sup>2</sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-forests_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forests-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The forest in the state can be broadly divided into four major biotic provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-flora_and_fauna_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flora_and_fauna-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> They are:
</p>
<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Deccan_Plateau" title="Deccan Plateau">Deccan Plateau</a></li>
<li>Central Plateau</li>
<li>Eastern Highland</li>
<li>East Coastal Plains</li></ol>
<p><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Ghats" title="Eastern Ghats">Eastern Ghats</a> region is home to dense tropical forests, while the vegetation becomes sparse as the Ghats give way to the Deccan Plateau, where shrub vegetation is more common. The vegetation found in the state is largely of dry deciduous types with a mixture of <a href="/wiki/Teak" title="Teak">teak</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Terminalia_(plant)" title="Terminalia (plant)">Terminalia</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dalbergia" title="Dalbergia">Dalbergia</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pterocarpus" title="Pterocarpus">Pterocarpus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Anogeissus" title="Anogeissus">Anogeissus</a></i>, etc.
</p><p>The state has many <a href="/wiki/Sanctuaries" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanctuaries">sanctuaries</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_parks" class="mw-redirect" title="National parks">national parks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zoo_Park" title="Zoo Park">zoological parks</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Coringa_Wildlife_Sanctuary" title="Coringa Wildlife Sanctuary">Coringa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krishna_Wildlife_Sanctuary" title="Krishna Wildlife Sanctuary">Krishna Wildlife Sanctuary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nagarjunsagar-Srisailam_Tiger_Reserve" title="Nagarjunsagar-Srisailam Tiger Reserve">Nagarjunsagar-Srisailam Tiger Reserve</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kambalakonda_Wildlife_Sanctuary" title="Kambalakonda Wildlife Sanctuary">Kambalakonda Wildlife Sanctuary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Venkateswara_Zoological_Park" title="Sri Venkateswara Zoological Park">Sri Venkateswara Zoological Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi_Zoological_Park" title="Indira Gandhi Zoological Park">Indira Gandhi Zoological Park</a>. <a href="/wiki/Atapaka_Bird_Sanctuary" class="mw-redirect" title="Atapaka Bird Sanctuary">Atapaka Bird Sanctuary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nelapattu_Bird_Sanctuary" title="Nelapattu Bird Sanctuary">Nelapattu Bird Sanctuary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pulicat_Lake_Bird_Sanctuary" title="Pulicat Lake Bird Sanctuary">Pulicat Lake Bird Sanctuary</a> attract many migratory birds.<sup id="cite_ref-lakes_and_wetlands_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lakes_and_wetlands-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
The state possesses some rare and endemic plants like <i><a href="/wiki/Cycas_beddomei" title="Cycas beddomei">Cycas beddomei</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pterocarpus_santalinus" title="Pterocarpus santalinus">Pterocarpus santalinus</a></i>, <i>Terminalia pallida</i>, <i>Syzygium alternifolium</i>, <i>Shorea talura</i>, <i>Shorea tumburgia</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Psilotum_nudum" title="Psilotum nudum">Psilotum nudum</a></i>, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-flora_and_fauna_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flora_and_fauna-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The diversity of fauna includes tigers, panthers, hyenas, black bucks, cheetals, sambars, sea turtles and a number of birds and reptiles. The estuaries of the Godavari and Krishna Rivers support rich mangrove forests with fishing cats and otters as keystone species.<sup id="cite_ref-flora_and_fauna_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flora_and_fauna-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The climate of Andhra Pradesh varies considerably, depending on the geographical region. Summers last from March to June. In the coastal plain, the summer temperatures are generally higher than the rest of the state, with temperature ranging between 20&#160;°C and 41&#160;°C. July to September is the season for tropical rains. About one-third of the total rainfall is brought by the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_monsoon" class="mw-redirect" title="Northeast monsoon">northeast monsoon</a>. October and November see low-pressure systems and tropical cyclones form in the Bay of Bengal which, along with the northeast monsoon, bring rains to the southern and coastal regions of the state.
</p><p>November, December, January, and February are the winter months in Andhra Pradesh. Since the state has a long coastal belt the winters are not very cold. The range of winter temperature is generally 12&#160;°C to 30&#160;°C. <a href="/wiki/Lambasingi" title="Lambasingi">Lambasingi</a>  in <a href="/wiki/Visakhapatnam_district" title="Visakhapatnam district">Visakhapatnam district</a> is the only place in South India which receives snowfall because of its location as at 1,000&#160;m (3,300&#160;ft) above the sea level. It is also nicknamed as the "Kashmir of Andhra Pradesh" and the temperature ranges from 0&#160;°C to 10&#160;°C.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Andhra_Pradesh" title="Ethnic groups of Andhra Pradesh">Ethnic groups of Andhra Pradesh</a></div>
<table class="infobox collapsible collapsed" style="float: right; padding: 1px; border-spacing: 0; text-align:right">
<tbody><tr>
<th colspan="4" style="padding-right: 3px; padding-left: 3px; text-align: center; font-size: 110%;">Population Trend&#160;</th></tr>
<tr style="font-size: 95%;">
<th style="text-align: center; border-bottom: 1px solid #000">Census</th><th style="text-align:center; border-bottom:1px solid black">Pop.</th><th style="text-align:center; border-bottom:1px solid black"> </th><th style="text-align:center; border-bottom:1px solid black">%±</th></tr>
<tr><td style="text-align:center"><b>1961</b></td><td style="padding-left:8px">35,983,000</td><td></td><td style="padding-left:8px"><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">—</div></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:center"><b>1971</b></td><td style="padding-left:8px">43,503,000</td><td></td><td style="padding-left:8px">20.9%</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:center"><b>1981</b></td><td style="padding-left:8px">53,550,000</td><td></td><td style="padding-left:8px">23.1%</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:center"><b>1991</b></td><td style="padding-left:8px">66,508,000</td><td></td><td style="padding-left:8px">24.2%</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:center"><b>2001</b></td><td style="padding-left:8px">75,727,000</td><td></td><td style="padding-left:8px">13.9%</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:center"><b>2011</b></td><td style="padding-left:8px">84,665,533</td><td></td><td style="padding-left:8px">11.8%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="4" style="border-top:1px solid black; font-size:85%; text-align:left"><i>Includes <a href="/wiki/Telangana" title="Telangana">Telangana</a>.</i><br />Source:Census of India<sup id="cite_ref-demographics_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p><br />
As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Census_of_India" title="Census of India">Census of India</a>, the state had a population of 49,386,799 with a population density of 308/km<sup>2</sup> (800/sq&#160;mi).
</p><p>According to Polavaram ordinance bill 2014, 7 mandals of Khammam district in Telangana state merged with Andhra Pradesh to facilitate Polavaram project, due to which population of 2,47,515 added to Andhra Pradesh. Thus the final population of Andhra Pradesh in the year 2014, as per census 2011 is 4,96,34,314, with a density of 304.5/km<sup>2</sup>.
</p><p>The total population constitute, 70.4% of rural population with 34,776,389 inhabitants and 29.6% of urban population with 14,610,410 inhabitants. Children in the age group of 0–6 years are 5,222,384, constituting 10.6% of the total population, among them 2,686,453 are boys and 2,535,931 are girls. <a href="/wiki/Visakhapatnam_district" title="Visakhapatnam district">Visakhapatnam district</a> has the largest urban population of 47.5% and <a href="/wiki/Srikakulam_district" title="Srikakulam district">Srikakulam district</a> with 83.8%, has the largest rural population, among others districts in the state. The overall population of the state comprises 17.1% of Scheduled Caste and 5.3% of Scheduled Tribe population.<sup id="cite_ref-profile_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-profile-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are 24,738,068 male and 24,648,731 female citizens—a <a href="/wiki/Human_sex_ratio" title="Human sex ratio">sex ratio</a> of 996 females per 1000 males, higher than the national average of 926 per 1000. The literacy rate of the state stands at 67.41%. However, Post bifurcation from <a href="/wiki/Telangana" title="Telangana">Telangana</a>, the state is expected to reach 91.1% by 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/West_Godavari_district" title="West Godavari district">West Godavari district</a> has the highest literacy rate of 74.6% and <a href="/wiki/Vizianagaram_district" title="Vizianagaram district">Vizianagaram district</a> has the least with 58.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-demographics_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-census_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Andhra Pradesh ranks tenth of all Indian States in the Human Development Index scores<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> with a score of 0.416. The National Council of Applied Economic Research district analysis in 2001 reveals that <a href="/wiki/Krishna_district" title="Krishna district">Krishna</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Godavari" class="mw-redirect" title="West Godavari">West Godavari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chittoor_district" title="Chittoor district">Chittoor</a> are the three districts in rural AP with the highest <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> scores in ascending order.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of Andhra Pradesh is <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">Telugu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-language_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-language-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nclmanurep2010_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nclmanurep2010-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The Minister of Tourism and Culture has issued a declaration of the Telugu language as a <a href="/wiki/Classical_languages_of_India#Classical" class="mw-redirect" title="Classical languages of India">Classical Language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Classical_Language_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Classical_Language-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions">Religions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Religions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">
<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:; background: white;">
<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">

<p>Majority of the people in Andhra Pradesh are Hindus while Muslims constitute a sizeable minority. According to the 2011 census, the major religious groups in the state are Hindus (90.87%), Muslims (7.32%) and Christians (1.38%). Buddhists, Sikhs, Jains and the people who declined to state their religion make up the remaining portion of population.<sup id="cite_ref-census2011_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2011-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hinduism">Hinduism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Hinduism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Venkateswara_Temple,_Tirumala" title="Venkateswara Temple, Tirumala">Venkateswara Temple</a> at <a href="/wiki/Tirupati" title="Tirupati">Tirupati</a> is the world's second-richest temple and is visited by millions of devotees throughout the year.
Andhra Pradesh is home to Shankaracharya of Pushpagiri Peetham. Other Hindu saints include <a href="/wiki/Sadasiva_Brahmendra" title="Sadasiva Brahmendra">Sadasiva Brahmendra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kannappa_Nayanar" class="mw-redirect" title="Kannappa Nayanar">Bhaktha Kannappa</a>, Yogi Vemana,  <a href="/wiki/Sathya_Sai_Baba" title="Sathya Sai Baba">Sathya Sai Baba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pothuluru_Veerabrahmendra" title="Pothuluru Veerabrahmendra">Pothuluru Veerabrahmendra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mahayana_Buddhism">Mahayana Buddhism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Mahayana Buddhism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Buddhism spread to Andhra Pradesh early in its history. The Krishna River valley was "a site of extraordinary Buddhist activity for almost a thousand years."<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The ancient Buddhist sites in the lower Krishna Valley, including Amaravati, Nagarjunakonda and Jaggayyapeta "can be traced to at least the third century BCE, if not earlier."<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The region played a central role in the development of <a href="/wiki/Mahayana_Buddhism" class="mw-redirect" title="Mahayana Buddhism">Mahayana Buddhism</a>, along with the <a href="/wiki/Magadha" title="Magadha">Magadha</a>-area in northeastern India.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/A.K._Warder" class="mw-redirect" title="A.K. Warder">A.K. Warder</a> holds that "the Mahāyāna originated in the south of India and almost certainly in the Andhra country."<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> According to Xing, "Several scholars have suggested that the Prajnaparamita probably developed among the Mahasamghikas in Southern India probably in the Andhra country, on the Krishna River."<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Praj%C3%B1%C4%81p%C4%81ramit%C4%81" class="mw-redirect" title="Prajñāpāramitā">Prajñāpāramitā</a> Sutras belong to the earliest <a href="/wiki/Mahayana_Sutras" class="mw-redirect" title="Mahayana Sutras">Mahayana Sutras</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions">Regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Regions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Andhra Pradesh comprises two regions: <a href="/wiki/Coastal_Andhra" title="Coastal Andhra">Coastal Andhra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rayalaseema" title="Rayalaseema">Rayalaseema</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Districts">Districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_districts_in_Andhra_Pradesh" title="List of districts in Andhra Pradesh">List of districts in Andhra Pradesh</a></div>
<p>It has a total of 13 districts,  nine in Coastal Andhra Region and four in Rayalaseema Region.
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 22em; -webkit-column-width: 22em; column-width: 22em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Anantapur_district" title="Anantapur district">Anantapur</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chittoor_district" title="Chittoor district">Chittoor</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/East_Godavari_district" class="mw-redirect" title="East Godavari district">East Godavari</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guntur_district" title="Guntur district">Guntur</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kadapa_district" title="Kadapa district">Kadapa</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Krishna_district" title="Krishna district">Krishna</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kurnool_district" title="Kurnool district">Kurnool</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prakasam_district" title="Prakasam district">Prakasam</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nellore_district" title="Nellore district">Nellore</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Srikakulam_district" title="Srikakulam district">Srikakulam</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Vizianagaram_district" title="Vizianagaram district">Vizianagaram</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/West_Godavari_district" title="West Godavari district">West Godavari</a><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Revenue_divisions">Revenue divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Revenue divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Revenue_Divisions_in_Andhra_Pradesh" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Revenue Divisions in Andhra Pradesh">List of Revenue Divisions in Andhra Pradesh</a></div>
<p>These 13 districts are further divided into 50 revenue divisions.
There are as many as 7 revenue divisions in East Godavari, and only 2 in Vizianagaram district.<sup id="cite_ref-profile_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-profile-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mandals">Mandals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Mandals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mandals_in_Andhra_Pradesh" title="List of mandals in Andhra Pradesh">List of mandals in Andhra Pradesh</a></div>
<p>The 50 revenue divisions are in turn divided into 671 <a href="/wiki/Mandals" class="mw-redirect" title="Mandals">mandals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fn1_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fn1-84">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> Chittoor district has the most <a href="/wiki/Tehsil" title="Tehsil">mandals</a> with 66 and Vizianagaram has the least with 34.<sup id="cite_ref-districts&amp;mandals_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-districts&amp;mandals-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cities">Cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are a total of <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Andhra_Pradesh" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities in Andhra Pradesh">31 cities</a> which include, <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipal_corporations_in_India" title="List of municipal corporations in India">16 municipal corporations</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Andhra_Pradesh" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities in Andhra Pradesh">14 municipalities</a>. There are two cities with <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_India_by_population" title="List of cities in India by population">more than one million</a> inhabitants, namely <a href="/wiki/Visakhapatnam" title="Visakhapatnam">Visakhapatnam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vijayawada" title="Vijayawada">Vijayawada</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Andhra_Pradesh" title="Government of Andhra Pradesh">Government of Andhra Pradesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Andhra_Pradesh" title="Politics of Andhra Pradesh">Politics of Andhra Pradesh</a></div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guntur_District_Court,_India.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Guntur_District_Court%2C_India.jpg/220px-Guntur_District_Court%2C_India.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Guntur_District_Court%2C_India.jpg/330px-Guntur_District_Court%2C_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Guntur_District_Court%2C_India.jpg/440px-Guntur_District_Court%2C_India.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guntur_District_Court,_India.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>District Court, Guntur</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eluru_District_Collector_Office.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Eluru_District_Collector_Office.jpg/220px-Eluru_District_Collector_Office.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Eluru_District_Collector_Office.jpg/330px-Eluru_District_Collector_Office.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Eluru_District_Collector_Office.jpg/440px-Eluru_District_Collector_Office.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1574" data-file-height="1015" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eluru_District_Collector_Office.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>West Godavari district Collectorate complex, Eluru</div></div></div>
<p>When the state was first created,  <a href="/wiki/Tanguturi_Prakasam" title="Tanguturi Prakasam">Tanguturi Prakasam Pantulu</a>, became the chief minister. After the unification with Telangana,  <a href="/wiki/Neelam_Sanjiva_Reddy" title="Neelam Sanjiva Reddy">Neelam Sanjiva Reddy</a>  became the first chief  minisiter.  He later served as president of India.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> After Telangana became  a separate state,  <a href="/wiki/Nara_Chandrababu_Naidu" class="mw-redirect" title="Nara Chandrababu Naidu">Nara Chandrababu Naidu</a>, the chief of the <a href="/wiki/Telugu_Desam_Party" title="Telugu Desam Party">Telugu Desam Party</a> became <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Minister">chief minister</a> on 8 June 2014, for the new state of Andhra Pradesh.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2014, <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Andhra_Pradesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative Assembly of Andhra Pradesh">Legislative Assembly of Andhra Pradesh</a> is the lower house of the state with 175 members and <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh_Legislative_Council" title="Andhra Pradesh Legislative Council">legislative council of andhra pradesh</a> is the upper house with 58 members. In the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_India" title="Parliament of India">Parliament of India</a>, Andhra Pradesh has 11 seats in the <a href="/wiki/Rajya_Sabha" title="Rajya Sabha">Rajya Sabha</a>, and 25 seats in the <a href="/wiki/Lok_Sabha" title="Lok Sabha">Lok Sabha</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> There are a total of 175 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Assembly_constituencies_of_Andhra_Pradesh" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Assembly constituencies of Andhra Pradesh">Assembly constituencies</a> in the state. <a href="/wiki/East_Godavari_district" class="mw-redirect" title="East Godavari district">East Godavari district</a> has the highest number of <a href="/wiki/Constituencies" class="mw-redirect" title="Constituencies">constituencies</a> with 19 and <a href="/wiki/Vizianagaram_district" title="Vizianagaram district">Vizianagaram district</a> has the least with 9 assembly seats.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Whereas, the legislative council of the state has 58 seats, which is one-third of total assembly seats.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Congress, the <a href="/wiki/Praja_Socialist_Party" title="Praja Socialist Party">Praja Socialist Party</a>  and the Krishi Lok Party were the major parties in the 1950s. Later the CPI became dominant opposition party. In the 1967 state assembly elections, all socialist parties were eliminated and <a href="/wiki/CPI" class="mw-redirect" title="CPI">CPI</a> lost opposition party status.
</p><p>Indian National Congress ruled the state from 1956 to 1982. In 1983, the <a href="/wiki/Telugu_Desam_Party" title="Telugu Desam Party">Telugu Desam Party</a> (TDP) won the state elections and <a href="/wiki/N.T._Rama_Rao" class="mw-redirect" title="N.T. Rama Rao">N.T. Rama Rao</a>(NTR) became the chief minister of the state for the first time. This broke the long time single party monopoly enjoyed by the INC. The 1989 elections ended the rule of <a href="/wiki/N._T._Rama_Rao" title="N. T. Rama Rao">NTR</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">INC</a> party returning to power with <a href="/wiki/Marri_Chenna_Reddy" title="Marri Chenna Reddy">Marri Chenna Reddy</a> at the helm. He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Nedurumalli_Janardhana_Reddy" class="mw-redirect" title="Nedurumalli Janardhana Reddy">Janardhan Reddy</a> in 1990, who was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Kotla_Vijaya_Bhaskara_Reddy" title="Kotla Vijaya Bhaskara Reddy">Kotla Vijaya Bhaskara Reddy</a> in 1992.
</p><p>In 1994, Andhra Pradesh gave a mandate to the <a href="/wiki/Telugu_Desam_Party" title="Telugu Desam Party">Telugu Desam Party</a> again, and <a href="/wiki/N._T._Rama_Rao" title="N. T. Rama Rao">NTR</a> became the chief minister again. Nara Chandrababu Naidu, the son-in-law of NTR, came to power in 1995 with the backing of a majority of the <a href="/wiki/MLAs" class="mw-redirect" title="MLAs">MLAs</a>. The Telugu Desam Party won both the assembly and <a href="/wiki/Lok_Sabha" title="Lok Sabha">Lok Sabha</a> election in 1999 under the leadership of Chandrababu Naidu. Thus <a href="/wiki/Nara_Chandrababu_Naidu" class="mw-redirect" title="Nara Chandrababu Naidu">N. Chandrababu Naidu</a> held the record for the longest-serving chief minister (1995 to 2004).<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In what would be the last elections held in the unified state in 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Telugu_Desam_Party" title="Telugu Desam Party">Telugu Desam Party</a> got a mandate in their favour in the residuary (new) state.  In 2019 Elections, <a href="/wiki/Y._S._Jaganmohan_Reddy" title="Y. S. Jaganmohan Reddy">Jaganmohan reddy</a> of <a href="/wiki/YSR_Congress_Party" title="YSR Congress Party">YSR Congress</a> became Chief Minister.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Andhra_Pradesh" title="Economy of Andhra Pradesh">Economy of Andhra Pradesh</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vizagcity.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Vizagcity.jpg/220px-Vizagcity.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Vizagcity.jpg/330px-Vizagcity.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Vizagcity.jpg/440px-Vizagcity.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="534" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vizagcity.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Visakhapatnam" title="Visakhapatnam">Visakhapatnam</a> is an important commercial hub of the state</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Visakhapatnam_view_from_Vizag_seaport.JPG" class="image"><img alt="seaport distance view" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Visakhapatnam_view_from_Vizag_seaport.JPG/220px-Visakhapatnam_view_from_Vizag_seaport.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Visakhapatnam_view_from_Vizag_seaport.JPG/330px-Visakhapatnam_view_from_Vizag_seaport.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Visakhapatnam_view_from_Vizag_seaport.JPG/440px-Visakhapatnam_view_from_Vizag_seaport.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Visakhapatnam_view_from_Vizag_seaport.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Visakhapatnam skyline, overlooking seaport</div></div></div>
<p>Andhra Pradesh was ranked eighth among other Indian states in terms of <a href="/wiki/Gross_state_product" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross state product">GSDP</a> for the financial year 2014–2015. The GSDP at current prices was <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>5,200.3 billion</span> (US$75&#160;billion) and at constant prices was <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>2,645.21 billion</span> (US$38&#160;billion).<sup id="cite_ref-gsdp_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gsdp-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The domestic product of agriculture sector accounts for <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>545.99 billion</span> (US$7.9&#160;billion) and industrial sector for <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>507.45 billion</span> (US$7.3&#160;billion). The service sector of the state accounts more percentage of the GSDP with a total of <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>1,305.87 billion</span> (US$19&#160;billion).<sup id="cite_ref-economy_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> In the 2010 list by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine, there were several from Andhra Pradesh among the top 100 richest Indians.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andhra_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 180.66666666667px"><div style="width: 180.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 178.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Konaseema_greenery_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e3/Konaseema_greenery_1.JPG/268px-Konaseema_greenery_1.JPG" decoding="async" width="179" height="134" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e3/Konaseema_greenery_1.JPG/403px-Konaseema_greenery_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e3/Konaseema_greenery_1.JPG/536px-Konaseema_greenery_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Lush green farms in <a href="/wiki/Konaseema" title="Konaseema">Konaseema</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Godavari_district" class="mw-redirect" title="East Godavari district">East Godavari</a>
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 146px"><div style="width: 146px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 144px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Sugar_industries_in_Andhra_Pradesh.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Map_of_Sugar_industries_in_Andhra_Pradesh.png/216px-Map_of_Sugar_industries_in_Andhra_Pradesh.png" decoding="async" width="144" height="134" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Map_of_Sugar_industries_in_Andhra_Pradesh.png/324px-Map_of_Sugar_industries_in_Andhra_Pradesh.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Map_of_Sugar_industries_in_Andhra_Pradesh.png/432px-Map_of_Sugar_industries_in_Andhra_Pradesh.png 2x" data-file-width="643" data-file-height="599" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Map of Sugar industries in Andhra Pradesh
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul>
